class=\"site-content\" role=\"main\">\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t<article id=\"post-130\" class=\"post-130 page type-page status-publish hentry\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<header class=\"entry-header\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<h1 class=\"entry-title\">About &amp; Our&nbsp;Criteria</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t</header><!-- .entry-header -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"entry-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<p><img src=\"http://cfile3.uf.tistory.com/image/23233844541FDC772C97A1\" alt=\"Image result for iu singing\"></p>\n<h1 style=\"text-align:left;\"><a href=\"http://kpopvocalanalysis.wordpress.com/categoryvocal-analyses/\">Vocal Analyses</a></h1>\n<h1 style=\"text-align:left;\"><a href=\"http://kpopvocalanalysis.wordpress.com/about-our-criteria-disclaimer/the-team/\"><strong>THE TEAM PAGE HERE</strong></a></h1>\n<h1 style=\"text-align:left;\"></h1>\n<h1 style=\"text-align:left;\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.wordpress.com/future-analyses\"><strong>FUTURE ANALYSES&nbsp;HERE</strong></a></h1>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">This blog was made with the intent to share knowledge and share vocal analyses from different vocalists in K-pop. Nobody in the blog is a hater or an anti-fan. The analyses give positive and negative points and are all constructive criticism, nobody is telling you to hate or not listen to your favorite idol vocalist. We’re only letting you know what their vocal skill based on what vocal technique and music theory is from a musically professional standpoint. If you’re confused about rankings, categories and such, click the about and our criteria page. This post will also include the information existing in that page if you’re unwilling to click through just click read more. Otherwise click About &amp; Our Criteria and most questions should be answered. We try to back up all our points with substantial evidence from the singers’ performances, we thoroughly listen to their performances from past and present. No one in this blog claims to be an expert, we’re all learning and everyday we learn more and more, just as we respect your opinions, please respect ours, which were influenced by the knowledge we have and the way we’ve been taught. Thank you.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalyses.files.wordpress.com/2014/04/cropped-header1.png\"><img data-attachment-id=\"938\" data-permalink=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/cropped-header1-png/\" data-orig-file=\"https://kpopvocalanalyses.files.wordpress.com/2014/04/cropped-header1.png\" data-orig-size=\"980,186\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"cropped-header1.png\" data-image-description=\"<p>http://kpopvocalanalysis.files.wordpress.com/2014/04/cropped-header1.png</p>\n\" data-medium-file=\"https://kpopvocalanalyses.files.wordpress.com/2014/04/cropped-header1.png?w=750&amp;h=140\" data-large-file=\"https://kpopvocalanalyses.files.wordpress.com/2014/04/cropped-header1.png?w=604\" class=\"wp-image-938 aligncenter\" src=\"https://kpopvocalanalyses.files.wordpress.com/2014/04/cropped-header1.png?w=750&amp;h=140\" alt=\"cropped-header1.png\" width=\"750\" height=\"140\" srcset=\"https://kpopvocalanalyses.files.wordpress.com/2014/04/cropped-header1.png?w=150&amp;h=28 150w, https://kpopvocalanalyses.files.wordpress.com/2014/04/cropped-header1.png?w=300&amp;h=57 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 750px) 100vw, 750px\"></a></p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">This blog is dedicated to compile vocal analyses done by our contributors in order to satisfy everyone’s curiosity regarding their idols’ vocal. The analysis will be based solely on&nbsp;<strong>VOCAL TECHNIQUE,&nbsp;</strong>not tone, timbre, emotions, stage presence, etc.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">The analysis might change according to their latest performance.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">If you would like your idol to be analyzed feel free to drop the question in the comment box. If you feel that the analysis is not accurate, you could suggest a video or recording and give us the reasoning behind your disagreement. We will gladly alter the vocal analysis page of the respective idol if your reasoning behind it is proven.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">Comments will be moderated. Constructive discussion are welcome. Bashful and hateful comments will be deleted. Every idol mentioned here are talented in their own way. Even so, we are focusing solely on their vocal capabilities and we try our best to give an objective analysis regarding the matters.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">So far, we will use this system as our judging criteria. We will elaborate more once it’s established. It goes from best to worst.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong><span style=\"color:#ff6600;\">TERMINOLOGY</span></strong></p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Tones/Semitones/Notes/Key<br>\n</strong>A key of a song means within the key signature of the song. There are 12 notes in total, C C#/Db D D#/Eb E F F#/Gb G G#/Ab A A#/Bb B and back to C, completing one full octave. A tone is from a note up two semitones, so the distance between C and C#/Db is a semitone, whereas C and D are a full note apart. A major Key will follow a tone tone semitone tone tone tone semitone pattern, so C major is C D E F G A B C. Although there are no sharps or flats between E and F or B and C, they’re a semitone apart. # stands for sharp and b stands for flat and whether or not you name a note sharp or flat depends on the key, i.e. C# major and Db major are the same key with different names, C# D# E# F# G# A# B# C# and Db Eb F Gb Ab Bb C Db, on a piano the same notes are played, just with different names.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Intonation<br>\n</strong>Being able to stay in pitch and in key. Good intonation means not going sharp, flat or singing a note that isn’t within the chord progression and/or key of the song. Going sharp means slightly above the pitch but not really hitting a note above, so like a note in between C and C#, and flat means a note that’s slightly below pitch, so a note in between C and B, for example.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Larynx Position/High Larynx/Low Larynx/Neutral Larynx<br>\n</strong>The larynx is the part of the body where the vocal cords are located. The vocal cords are very small and are divided into two parts that vibrate against one another in order to create sound. The speed of the vibration generally determines the pitch someone sings in. Much like tuning a guitar, the more stretched the vocal cords are and thinner they become, the higher the pitch and the thicker they are, the lower the pitch is. In order for a note to be hit, one should have a relaxed opened sound in the larynx, without any restrictions from the throat muscles. If the larynx is pushed down, it creates a froggy and fake “soulful” tone, if it’s pulled up, it creates a thinner, squeezed and tight quality to the voice. The natural state of the larynx is being neutral when it’s relaxed, if it’s forced either up or down, that means the muscles in the throat are creating tension and the larynx is trying to reposition itself in an uncomfortable and unnatural position to hit notes that are not within the individual’s supported range.&nbsp;<strong><br>\n</strong></p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Tonality/Tone Production<br>\n</strong>The way tone and sound is produced through good support. The voice comes out stable, without any laryngeal restriction nor tension, tone is clean and has the true sound of the individual’s voice type, without an uncentered pitch, excessive breathiness, nasality and tension.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Vibrato<br>\n</strong>The shift between two notes rapidly within, normally, a sustained note. The difference between the notes is usually less than a semitone. A forced throaty vibrato is usually produced artificially by using the throat, instead of the natural vibrato that comes out once the vocal cords are relaxed with good breath support.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Stability<br>\n</strong>The stability of the voice, meaning it’s not off pitch and it doesn’t sound wobbly, shaky and unsupported.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Registers<br>\n</strong>Chest voice, lowest range. Head voice, highest range. Mixed voice, the belting area of the voice.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Support<br>\n</strong>How the individual vocalist uses their correct breathing technique with the diaphragm to better support, project and hold their voice together.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Placement vs Resonance vs Projection<br>\n</strong>Resonance is the optimum sound a vocalist should focus on when singing. It is a full, clean and round sound that won’t sound thin, constricted or small. A vocalist who’s resonant will use different types of placements, i.e. their voice will be placed either in their chest, head or mask (cheekbones area, not nose) to project their voice, in each individual register. A vocalist may be able to be resonant in their mixed voice by normally placing their voice in their mask with chest resonance, or as they go higher, with head resonance. A resonant sound is always going to be a projected sound, now resonance doesn’t mean loud, because a loud sound may still be pushed and strained. You may project but still have tension, but in true resonance tension should not be present. Resonance is produced when the vocalist is able to support their voice. In other words, they have developed vocal cords that are able to connect fully in a healthy manner, without breathiness coming between them nor too much constriction, against the right amount of air pressure. Then the supported sound is enhanced with the proper placement of sound, while keeping the soft palate lifted, the larynx position not high, the swallowing muscles, jaw, tongue And throat relaxed and the jaw dropped so as to amplify the sound of the voice. The combination of an open throat, support, relaxed singing and proper placement is what creates healthy resonance in singing.&nbsp;</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Vocal Range vs Supported Range vs Tessitura<br>\n</strong>Vocal range means the individual’s lowest singable note to the individual’s highest singable note. &nbsp;A tessitura will depend on the individual’s voice type and where their voice sits most comfortably, shines the most and could project the best. A supported range includes notes outside the tessitura where the individual’s voice type may not be naturally inclined to project well in, however so due to the vocalist’s own ability, they’re able to still maintain tone production, support, projection and stability. e.g In classical music, sopranos’ tessituras are something in between A3/C4 to &nbsp;A5/C6, however in contemporary music a soprano singing as high as C6 is very uncommon and unnecessary; a contemporary soprano, for an example Luna, is able to keep resonance consistently up until Eb5, which is almost ideal for a soprano who should be able to carry that resonance up until A5 without a problem. However so she’s also able to sing down to G3 with correct support, which although is outside her voice type’s natural tessitura, she’s still able to keep support and projection down there.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Musicianship/Musicality<br>\n</strong>Musicianship is the act of changing any song given to you and making it your own, usually on the spot. This includes melodic changes, rhythmic changes and added embellishments. Musicality is the act of interpreting music correctly according to each individual genre of music, by adding the correct use of vocal effects (e.g. raspiness, breathiness, growls, vocal runs, vibrato) and playing with the song musically by adding dynamics (e.g. singing softly, loudly, powerfully on the right moments of each song).</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Passaggi/Vocal Bridges<br>\n</strong>A passaggio or a vocal bridge is an area of the voice where one’s voices transition naturally from one to the other in the modal register. Usually for males, the distance between the first passaggio, from chest voice to mixed voice, and the second passaggio, from mixed voice to head voice, is only about a 4th apart, whereas for females it’s about an octave apart. Passaggi are important for one to be able to tell what someone’s voice type is. A register break or the highest note you can sing in your chest/mixed voice before transitioning into head voice is NOT your first passaggio. The first passaggio is a note in your range where your voice naturally feels a switch of muscle coordination in your vocal cords. That doesn’t mean you can’t bring a chest dominant or balanced mixed voice above your first or even second passaggio. Lyric tenors usually have their passaggi around D4/Eb4 and G4/Ab4, whereas lyric baritones have their passaggi at B3 and E4. Lyric sopranos are usually at F4/F#4 and F5/F#5.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Legato/Staccato<br>\n</strong>A musical phrase usually will last a couple of bars. During a phrase, the melody may be played/sung smoothly connected without every note sounding chopped up, whereas staccato means emphasizing every single note separately with minor less than a second breaks in between every note. Legato is the most basic form of singing through correct breath control and support.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Agility<br>\n</strong>Vocal agility is an embellishment and it means, being able to sing many notes accurately and quickly, by separating each individual note while still being able to connect them within one sung vowel. Those are usually called melismas or vocal runs.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong><span style=\"color:#ff6600;\">CRITERIA</span></strong></p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Excellent Vocalist</strong></p>\n<ul style=\"text-align:left;\">\n<li>All three registers are developed</li>\n<li>Supported as close as possible from their highest to lowest extremities</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for sopranos falls somewhere within C3 ~ E3 (or lower) and G5 (or higher)</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for mezzo-sopranos falls somewhere within Bb2 ~ D3 (or lower) and F5 (or higher)</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice&nbsp;for tenors&nbsp;falls somewhere&nbsp;within F#2 ~ A2 (or lower) and&nbsp;C5/C#5 (or higher)</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for baritones&nbsp;falls somewhere within D2 ~ F#2 (or lower) and A4/Bb4 (or higher)</li>\n<li>Within their Voice Type’s tessitura they are consistently&nbsp;resonant</li>\n<li>Complete support in the middle register&nbsp;and lower register</li>\n<li>For females head voice must be completely resonant at will; for males head voice must be completely supported</li>\n<li>Connection in the voice with no noticeable breaks when transitions are being made</li>\n<li>Agility is present and pitch is controlled with good separation between individual note, potentially very complex runs are done from the bottom to the top of their ranges</li>\n<li>Musicianship the ability to change a song and make it their own and Musicality having complete control over the voice in any given genre</li>\n<li>Almost perfect intonation</li>\n<li>Tonality&nbsp;is almost never lost</li>\n</ul>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Great&nbsp;</strong></p>\n<ul style=\"text-align:left;\">\n<li>Developed registers, but one register may be lacking in development</li>\n<li>Optimal&nbsp;resonance is achieved on a regular basis</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice&nbsp;for sopranos falls somewhere within F3/F#3 and&nbsp;F#5/G5</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for mezzo-sopranos falls somewhere within Eb3/E3 and E5</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice&nbsp;for tenors&nbsp;falls somewhere&nbsp;within A2/Bb2&nbsp;and&nbsp;B4/C5</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for baritones&nbsp;falls somewhere within F#2/G2 and G#4/A4</li>\n<li>Support is present in all registers, but maybe not to their lowest and highest extremes</li>\n<li>Within in their voice type’s tessitura they are resonant and&nbsp;well projected, but not as resonant and&nbsp;well projected as Excellent vocalist</li>\n<li>Connection in the voice with no noticeable breaks</li>\n<li>Agility is present and pitch is controlled with good separation between individual notes</li>\n<li>Great interpretation skills (Musicianship), but Musicality may not be as finely tuned as Excellent vocalist</li>\n<li>Intonation is almost perfect</li>\n<li>Tonality is almost never lost</li>\n</ul>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Good&nbsp;</strong></p>\n<ul style=\"text-align:left;\">\n<li>One very well developed register or two well developed registers, with the others either being Average or Above Average</li>\n<li>Able to sing through their first passaggio&nbsp;and second passaggi with support and resonance, and above</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice&nbsp;for sopranos falls somewhere within F#3/G3&nbsp;and E5/F5</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for mezzo-sopranos falls somewhere within E3/F3 and D5/Eb5</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice&nbsp;for tenors&nbsp;falls somewhere&nbsp;within Bb2/B2/C3 and&nbsp;Bb4/B4</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for baritones&nbsp;falls somewhere within G2/G#2 and F#4/G4</li>\n<li>Optimal resonance often present, but is not always achieved</li>\n<li>Within their vocal type’s tessitura they are resonant and supported, but tonality can be lost at times.</li>\n<li>Connection between registers is not always present</li>\n<li>Some agility, but runs and transitions are not always controlled</li>\n<li>Interpretation skills are present, has show musicality</li>\n<li>Good intonation rarely goes off</li>\n<li>At times can lose tonality by rarely does</li>\n</ul>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Proficient&nbsp;</strong></p>\n<ul style=\"text-align:left;\">\n<li>One well developed or two/three somewhat developed register well balanced</li>\n<li>Able to sing through their first passaggio&nbsp;and second passaggi with support and resonance</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for sopranos falls somewhere within&nbsp;G#3/A3 and D5/Eb5</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for mezzo-sopranos falls somewhere within F#3 and C5/C#5</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for tenors&nbsp;falls somewhere&nbsp;within C3/C#3 and G#4/A4</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for baritones&nbsp;falls somewhere within G#2/A2 and E4/F4</li>\n<li>Consistently supported within their supported range</li>\n<li>Resonates at times, but optimal resonance is not a regular occurrence</li>\n<li>Connection between the registers is not present</li>\n<li>Intonation is not perfect, off-key moments happen at times</li>\n<li>Good tonality isn’t always kept, strain and tension are apparent at times</li>\n</ul>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Above Average</strong></p>\n<ul style=\"text-align:left;\">\n<li>One somewhat developed register with the others being average or weak</li>\n<li>Able to sing through their first passaggio with consistent support and possible resonance up to their second passaggio</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for sopranos falls somewhere within A3 and C5/C#5</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for mezzo-sopranos falls somewhere within G3 and B4/C5</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for tenors&nbsp;falls somewhere within&nbsp;D3 and G4/G#4</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for baritones&nbsp;falls somewhere within Bb2/B2 and Eb4/E4</li>\n<li>Inconsistent with resonance</li>\n<li>Even in their supported range strain and tension can be present</li>\n<li>Nasality can be present within the voice at times</li>\n<li>Intonation issues can be frequent</li>\n</ul>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Average</strong></p>\n<ul style=\"text-align:left;\">\n<li>No register is developed considerably well</li>\n<li>Able to sing through their first passaggio with adequate and consistent support</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for sopranos falls somewhere within&nbsp;Bb3 and Bb4/B4</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for mezzo-sopranos falls somewhere within G#3 and A4</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for tenors falls somewhere within&nbsp;Eb3 and F4/F#4</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for baritones&nbsp;falls somewhere within C3/C#3 and C#4/D4</li>\n<li>Inconsistent with support, and if at all resonance, even if occasional resonance has happened</li>\n<li>Good tonality is not present at all times, nasal placement is normally used</li>\n<li>Frequent intonation issues</li>\n</ul>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><strong>Weak</strong></p>\n<ul style=\"text-align:left;\">\n<li>No developed registers</li>\n<li>Unable to sing through their first passaggio with adequate and consistent support</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for sopranos falls somewhere within&nbsp;B3 and G#4/A4 (or less)</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for mezzo-sopranos falls somewhere within A3 and F#4 (or less)</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for tenors&nbsp;falls somewhere within E3/F3 and Eb4/E4 (or less)</li>\n<li>Range wise, supported range without head voice for baritones&nbsp;falls somewhere within C#3/D3 and B3/C4/C#4 (or less)</li>\n<li>Very inconsistent with support, strain,no resonance</li>\n<li>Good tonality is not present</li>\n<li>Out off tune singing is frequent</li>\n</ul>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">FYI, Among KPOP idols there is&nbsp;<b><span style=\"text-decoration:underline;\">NO ONE</span>&nbsp;</b>who is considered Excellent/Amazing/Fantastic vocal-wise (Imagine Maria Callas, Mariah Carey, Natalie Weiss and Whitney Houston as amazing/fantastic). They are Great/Good at best.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">For further question you can ask the contributors directly at this forum</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\"><a href=\"http://onehallyu.com/index.php?/topic/552-official-vocals-thread/\">OneHallyu vocals’ thread</a></p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">Regards,</p>\n<p style=\"text-align:left;\">Admin</p>\n<h1><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.wordpress.com/future-analyses\"><strong>FUTURE ANALYSES&nbsp;HERE</strong></a></h1>\n<h1><a href=\"http://kpopvocalanalysis.wordpress.com/about-our-criteria-disclaimer/the-team/\"><strong>THE TEAM PAGE HERE</strong></a></h1>\n\t\t<div class=\"wpcnt\">\n\t\t\t<div class=\"wpa wpmrec\" style=\"display: inline-block !important;\">\n\t\t\t\t<span class=\"wpa-about\">Advertisements</span>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"u\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<script type=\"text/javascript\">\n\t\t\t\t(function(g){if(\"undefined\"!=typeof g.__ATA){g.__ATA.initAd({sectionId:1155897811, width:300, height:250});}})(window);\n\t\t\t</script><div id=\"automattic-id-2095\" data-section=\"1155897811\" style=\"width: 300px; Our&nbsp;Criteria</span>”\t\t</h2>\n\n\t\t<ol class=\"comment-list\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<li id=\"comment-38816\" class=\"comment even thread-even depth-1 parent highlander-comment\">\n\t\t\t<article id=\"div-comment-38816\" class=\"comment-body\">\n\t\t\t\t<footer class=\"comment-meta\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-author vcard\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt=\"\" src=\"https://1.gravatar.com/avatar/ad0118b937f3a0a0839860426c50ff3d?s=74&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=G\" class=\"avatar avatar-74 grav-hashed grav-hijack\" height=\"74\" width=\"74\" id=\"grav-ad0118b937f3a0a0839860426c50ff3d-0\">\t\t\t\t\t\t<b class=\"fn\">Knock Knock</b> <span class=\"says\">says:</span>\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-author -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-metadata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-38816\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-14T03:29:08+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 14, 2017 at 3:29 am\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"jetpack-video-wrapper\"><span class=\"embed-youtube\" style=\"text-align:center; I’ll only answer it because I’ve seen it. She was showing off, she lacked musicality. There was no reason for her to sing those notes, except to show off. She was constantly pushing her larynx down for her low notes and raising her larynx for the high notes, so she was constantly straining throughout. The whistle register is impressive only if it’s done well, just being able to do it isn’t all that.</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-38843\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes you want to reach the level of excellent vocalists like sohyang?</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-38857\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a class=\"avatar avatar-74 grav-hashed grav-hijack\" height=\"74\" width=\"74\" id=\"grav-02dcf75f6bd3999e2cb9fe85ab48cf6e-3\">\t\t\t\t\t\t<b class=\"fn\">ahmin3</b> <span class=\"says\">says:</span>\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-author -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-metadata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-38880\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-15T10:36:06+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 15, 2017 at 10:36 am\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>If you notice something in our blog, we have no vocalist under the age of 25 who’s rated above the “Good to Great” rating. There is a reason for that. Training your voice takes time, your voice needs to mature and you need to be able to practice for years. It’s unfair to expect a vocalist to be able to become excellent within 2 to 3 years, given that great vocalists are usually closer to their 30’s. So I personally don’t think it’s a realistic amount of time, but it also depends on everybody’s level of skill when they start these “2 to 3 years.”</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-38880\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=38880&amp;_wpnonce=6614ff8c7d\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-38880\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</article><!-- .comment-body -->\n</li><!-- #comment-## -->\n</ol><!-- .children -->\n</li><!-- #comment-## -->\n</ol><!-- .children -->\n</li><!-- #comment-## -->\n\t\t<li id=\"comment-38844\" class=\"comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 parent highlander-comment\">\n\t\t\t<article id=\"div-comment-38844\" class=\"comment-body\">\n\t\t\t\t<footer class=\"comment-meta\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-author vcard\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt=\"\" src=\"https://1.gravatar.com/avatar/d524c4334065cb923c957d93959ae6b6?s=74&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=G\" class=\"avatar avatar-74 grav-hashed grav-hijack\" height=\"74\" width=\"74\" id=\"grav-d524c4334065cb923c957d93959ae6b6-0\">\t\t\t\t\t\t<b class=\"fn\">Mahdi</b> <span class=\"says\">says:</span>\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-author -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-metadata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-38844\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-14T21:14:18+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 14, 2017 at 9:14 pm\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>Hi~</p>\n<div class=\"jetpack-video-wrapper\"><span class=\"embed-youtube\" style=\"text-align:center; Is this the first time I hear you sing? I actually do hear a very nice connection in your head voice, although it could be more opened. I’d rather hear you singing throughout more of your range than to talk about support with you for now. You do have very good connection, even in your mix but the mixed Eb4 or E4 had a bit of a shouty quality to it. There’s no such thing as a light lyric baritone. Also you don’t sound like a tenor, you mix like a baritone. You’re not really nasal but you push a bit. Your mixing is actually balanced enough, so you have less issues than I’m used to hearing but I’d rather hear you singing a song that’s not an upbeat girl song down the octave.</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-38889\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=38889&amp;_wpnonce=025932bf3b\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-38889\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"reply\"><a rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"comment-reply-link\" href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?replytocom=38889#respond\" onclick=\"return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-38889&quot;, &quot;38889&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;130&quot; href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-38931\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-16T12:25:27+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 16, 2017 at 12:25 pm\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>Oh yeah that’s good, cause I don’t remember hearing you sing. Actually if you a song that’s a ballad, but a high female song, that’s fine for a baritone. It won’t sound as good as the female version because F#2 ~ F#4 is a lot less challenging for you than F#3 ~ F#5 for Beyoncé. But it is a better range to focus on your technique, now I still would rather hear you singing more in a mid range first but since you’re sending me full songs, I prefer this than listening to you singing 30 seconds of a song, and only the climax. It isn’t all about high notes. </p>\n<p>I would ask that you’d be a bit more understanding of us in the future and post less covers at once, since it can be quite time consuming.</p>\n<p>Listen:<br>\nYou’re not dropping your jaw low enough, you’re a bit in your nose. 0:30 you’re letting the sound be too low and you’re not keeping it forward enough. 0:41 0:45 careful with your runs. 0:36 and 0:50 you’re not Mariah Carey down the octave, don’t sing like you are. Don’t do the whole tone fade away into a sexy whispery sound, because I know Mariah so I can tell where this influence is coming from. I’m not saying it’s a bad thing, but it’s a bad habit of emulating her style, you’re too heavy and a bit too loud actually. It might be that you’re too close to the mic. 1:09 ~ 1:13 lots of tongue tension, 1:14 1:17 careful with these runs, you’re adlibbing too much throughout. It’s nice that you have those musical ideas, but you have to be clean and commit to them. You have to really be clean, be precise, you shouldn’t just throw in random musical ideas and hope they land. They have to really be 100% sure. 2:08 ~ 2:10 nice melodic change, I really like your ideas. 2:19 This is weird because in your other audios you’re so much brighter and lighter, but you’re so heavy and chesty in this. It’s a very different quality of tone than your other audios. 3:03 too wide, your vowels are way too wide. You need to drop your jaw, not since with your lips spread out. The harmonies at the end would be really nice, if you were in the same room. 3:35 again those R&amp;B He-he-he sounds, it doesn’t work if you’re not 100% precise. 3:58 again musically, you can just sing the song. You don’t need to throw runs everywhere to prove anything. When you sing so many runs out of context, it feels like you’re trying to prove something. Runs are used to embellish songs, not to show off.</p>\n<p>My All:<br>\nThis song is even more dangerous, cause this song has a lot of runs naturally. 0:37 again all those H’s, 0:44 dropping the larynx, sliding. This is literally Mariah. You have a very nice tone, it shows in the chorus, but it gets lost in you trying to emulate another vocalist. If you were a girl, it could work a bit better even though I still wouldn’t encourage it. But if you’re a baritone with such a heavy voice singing a female song down the octave, it just sounds out of place. 1:52 again all those H’s that are not in the words, that’s pushing too much air. You’re not using your vocal cords. 2:10 See you have a very nice tone, I really like it actually. I want you to try singing one of these female songs in the right key for your voice once. I would raise it a minor or a major third. So for this one, I would say that you should sing it a couple of keys higher, 4 semitones.</p>\n<p>Also in the future don’t send me audios from smule, they’re stressful because you have to people who are not physically with each other trying to solo their way out of a song and it’s just kind of messy. I’d rather hear you on vocaroo by yourself, cause then I can focus on you. You also don’t even need to sing a whole song, just a verse and a chorus are fine.</p>\n<p>All Of Me:<br>\nYay a solo. lol 0:23 too much airiness, 0:26 late. You’re dragging the tempo. You’re behind the beat to an extent. Again stop adlibbing without a reason, 0:29 that was nice the first time around but then you did exactly the same thing at 0:45 and then it starts to get old and you’re not surprising the listener anymore. You have very good pitch, I hear tongue tension. It also comes with having an accent in English. Your head voice transitions are really nicee actually. 1:23 Don’t use H to push air so that you can sing higher, support. Don’t push air. Your head voice transitions are very nice and smooth, they’re really really good. You’re not dropping your jaw enough, so your sound kind of stays stuck in the back of your throat. You’re right though, All Of Me is a baritone song. You’re changing the timing and rhythm of so many of the phrases, it seems like you’re not sure of the lyrics and the actual rhythm and it can sound a bit awkward. This is indeed the best for a couple of reasons. It’s a song in the right key for your voice. It’s a solo so you’re not trying to sing all over someone else. Can you not mix above F#4? 3:56 again adding those H’s.<br>\nYour head voice is definitely your biggest strength. Cause All Of Me is supposed to have mixed G#4’s, but you head voiced them all. You had a chesty F#4 in Listen, but you only went up to F4 in the other songs. 4:42 again the runs, they have to have some sort of musical direction, not just showing off. I can hear the Mariah influence everywhere.</p>\n<p>Okay so what I conclude is that you have a lot of potential but then you have a lot of influences that take away from you singing like yourself and you end trying to emulate other people a lot. You have great musical ideas, but lack precision. Your placement is too low and you lack openness. Your diction comes from an accent which can hinder your openness and the vowel shapes. You have good pitch, you have a really voice. How do you practice singing? Do you do any exercises ever?</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-38931\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=38931&amp;_wpnonce=dd76aa2cf2\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-38931\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</article><!-- .comment-body -->\n</li><!-- #comment-## -->\n</ol><!-- .children -->\n</li><!-- #comment-## -->\n\t\t<li id=\"comment-38969\" class=\"comment even depth-2 parent highlander-comment\">\n\t\t\t<article id=\"div-comment-38969\" class=\"comment-body\">\n\t\t\t\t<footer class=\"comment-meta\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-author vcard\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt=\"\" src=\"https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/ed820a9f06d1a774778156275325fb30?s=74&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=G\" class=\"avatar avatar-74 grav-hashed grav-hijack\" height=\"74\" width=\"74\" id=\"grav-ed820a9f06d1a774778156275325fb30-2\">\t\t\t\t\t\t<b class=\"fn\">Hunter</b> <span class=\"says\">says:</span>\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-author -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-metadata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-38969\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-17T06:03:55+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 17, 2017 at 6:03 am\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>Oh, I didn’t think about the Mariah influence but yes she’s my #1 influence for vocals and such. Actually, if you listen to my older covers (don’t do that please), I didn’t know one clue about vocal technique. I sounded like a mess, nasal, throaty and husky literally shooting my larynx up for straining like a goat (I had a heady mix and shouted some awful G5/A5). I hated my voice so I came across those vocals videos and my first influence was Jennifer Hudson (lmao). My voice didn’t get better so I tried singing like Mariah Carey because everyone would said “oh she’s the better singer in this world” and things like this. I finally ended this not so long ago and started listening other artists like Brandy, JoJo, Hyorin etc. Tbh I honestly thought my voice was high-pitched and you’re the first person who said that I have a heavy voice lol. I realised I had a masculine voice and started listening male singers so I try to stop the Mariah Carey style but most of the time, I just can’t! I also try to stop with throwing adlibs everywhere but I think that’s the only thing I like in my voice so I won’t really stop this lol just properly placing them. For the mixing thing, I can mix above F#4, and in a good day, I’m comfortable mixing around D5/E5. I just don’t like belting around my passagio tbh I do this sometimes but since All Of Me is not really a belting song lol I didn’t really mix and I also try to stop belting above B4 because the term support is always misused in the vocal community and I don’t want to lose my voice lol. I watched your video though but it’s just so hard to get. In the Million Reasons cover, I briefly belted a Eb5 but the quality is awful. I definitely go with my head voice (or a heady mix) when I’m not sure if I’ll hit the notes if I mix though. For the All Of Me cover, I literally heard the song 2 times and it wasn’t the original version but a cover by Fifth Harmony lmao that’s why I was lost. I practice singing most of the time, and in my room. I entered at the Music Club of my highschool not long ago. For me, singing is not a hobby, it’s a huge part in my life, I always listen to different types of music (K-Pop, RNB, EDM, Rap, Ballad, Soul etc) and it’s mainly what helps me to live. I often do exercices like the ‘baby ba’ for the support and the brrrr sound but that’s all. I also do personnalised agility exercises, try to reduce jaw tension when doing them (even if I don’t do this at all) and tries to stop the use of falsetto. Most of the time, I just don’t do exercises but can you recommand me on what I should do for reducing my problems? Anyway, thanks for all the tips you gave to me, I’ll try reducing those problems and I’ll post a little clip (or two) for seeing how much I improved. And aw thanks for your compliments it’s really important for me! Bye! (Sorry for the lenghty post again, and the faults too <img draggable=\"false\" class=\"emoji\" alt=\"😓\" src=\"https://s0.wp.com/wp-content/mu-plugins/wpcom-smileys/twemoji/2/svg/1f613.svg\">)</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-38969\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=38969&amp;_wpnonce=d106b6adf5\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-38969\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"reply\"><a rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"comment-reply-link\" href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?replytocom=38969#respond\" onclick=\"return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-38969&quot;, &quot;38969&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;130&quot; Well by heavy I mean you’re not a light lyric soprano, aka Mariah, Hyorin, etc. So you are a man and a baritone so by definition your vocal cords are much thicker than theirs, so you have a heavier voice. I’d be interested to hear you mixing Eb5 as it could be a mask placed head voice. (Although I do know baritones who can shout mix like D5 and I just can’t shout for my life, so I can’t do that.) Well if singing is a huge part of your life and you like it, you have a really nice voice so I’d encourage you to not only keep singing but to also look into getting vocal lessons and working on the basics. Go one step at a time, going for Mariah as a beginner can be a bit much. You should do the light two note Ba exercise to work on proper vocal stretch, placement and openness. I’d rather you show me yourself doing exercises first before you send me anymore singing covers, actually. haha No problem, you’re welcome! ^ ^</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-38982\" She can’t support her voice in the fifth octave. She is constantly belting E5’s and G5’s, which only like 5 female idol sopranos can actually support, so it isn’t reasonable to expect anybody to just be able to hit those notes well. They are hard notes and high, so it makes no sense for us to focus on them singing that high. It’s important to listen to them in a mid range first, then if they can handle that, we can focus on expanding that.</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-38877\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=38877&amp;_wpnonce=f4276bf76e\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-38877\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"reply\"><a rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"comment-reply-link\" href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?replytocom=38877#respond\" onclick=\"return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-38877&quot;, &quot;38877&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;130&quot; )\" aria-label=\"Reply to ahmin3\">Reply</a></div>\t\t\t</article><!-- .comment-body -->\n<ol class=\"children\">\n\t\t<li id=\"comment-38881\" class=\"comment even depth-3 parent highlander-comment\">\n\t\t\t<article id=\"div-comment-38881\" class=\"comment-body\">\n\t\t\t\t<footer class=\"comment-meta\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-author vcard\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt=\"\" src=\"https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/5df0a6faabe72a519a005a74e5944f4b?s=74&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=G\" class=\"avatar avatar-74 grav-hashed grav-hijack\" height=\"74\" width=\"74\" id=\"grav-5df0a6faabe72a519a005a74e5944f4b-1\">\t\t\t\t\t\t<b class=\"fn\">Theo Engleton</b> <span class=\"says\">says:</span>\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-author -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-metadata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-38881\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-15T11:42:36+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 15, 2017 at 11:42 am\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>I see. A lot of airiness and a slightly high larynx here and there. The placement is very much in the mask, but without openness from the back of the throat. She overpronounces her R’s which really gets in the way of her singing, because she is really not focusing on her vowels. She focuses too much on the consonants. Of course I understand she has a Vietnamese accent, so it gets in the way of her singing. She has pretty good pitch, but she doesn’t really open up her sound at all and she kind of sounds cute throughout. It’s cute, bright, light and small throughout. She lacks openness, she doesn’t drop her jaw, she doesn’t mix very high, the range is limited. This is a cute cover though.<br>\nAnd yes you’re welcome to sing a language that’s more comfortable for you.</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-38929\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes Yes indeed Shownu is daddy. 0:12 too much of an H sound. 0:14 Creaking. You’re not Britney Spears down the octave, don’t emulate her this much. You’re definitely not tone deaf, you have a very nice voice actually. But the thing is, you’re trying to sing like a girl down the octave without a high larynx, which is good, but the whole breathiness, creaking, cracking on purpose, it’s all very Britney and it works for her but when other people do it, it’s kind of odd. “But you’ll see that, you’re the only one” that at the end was the only time you went into the fourth octave, where you hit C4 and D4. Try doing vocal exercises from the support video, two notes, that’s all it takes to build up a foundation of vocal stretch and technique. Watch the video to be sure. You’ll be able to create a better placed sound with better connection. Overall you were singing from Bb2 ~ D4 throughout the audio, so no, you’re definitely not a tenor. You’re a baritone.</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-38983\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=38983&amp;_wpnonce=44fd1f2e44\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-38983\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"reply\"><a rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"comment-reply-link\" href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?replytocom=38983#respond\" onclick=\"return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-38983&quot;, &quot;38983&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;130&quot; )\" aria-label=\"Reply to ahmin3\">Reply</a></div>\t\t\t</article><!-- .comment-body -->\n<ol class=\"children\">\n\t\t<li id=\"comment-38984\" class=\"comment odd alt depth-3 highlander-comment\">\n\t\t\t<article id=\"div-comment-38984\" class=\"comment-body\">\n\t\t\t\t<footer class=\"comment-meta\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-author vcard\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt=\"\" src=\"https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/0b2b059ec61162a97cd0730e503f48bd?s=74&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=G\" class=\"avatar avatar-74 grav-hashed grav-hijack\" height=\"74\" width=\"74\" id=\"grav-0b2b059ec61162a97cd0730e503f48bd-1\">\t\t\t\t\t\t<b class=\"fn\">buffyuna</b> <span class=\"says\">says:</span>\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-author -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-metadata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-38984\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-17T09:46:55+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 17, 2017 at 9:46 am\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>Yes it was my first time posting a singing clip! )\" aria-label=\"Reply to Baruc\">Reply</a></div>\t\t\t</article><!-- .comment-body -->\n<ol class=\"children\">\n\t\t<li id=\"comment-39011\" class=\"comment byuser comment-author-ahmin3 odd alt depth-2 highlander-comment\">\n\t\t\t<article id=\"div-comment-39011\" class=\"comment-body\">\n\t\t\t\t<footer class=\"comment-meta\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-author vcard\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt=\"\" src=\"https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/02dcf75f6bd3999e2cb9fe85ab48cf6e?s=74&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=G\" class=\"avatar avatar-74 grav-hashed grav-hijack\" height=\"74\" width=\"74\" id=\"grav-02dcf75f6bd3999e2cb9fe85ab48cf6e-18\">\t\t\t\t\t\t<b class=\"fn\">ahmin3</b> <span class=\"says\">says:</span>\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-author -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-metadata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-39011\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-18T00:17:54+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 18, 2017 at 12:17 am\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>Oi~ Sabe tem muita coisa que tem que ser feita para arrumar os problemas que você tem. Porque você tá cantando um pouco mais alto, você tem a idéia de que mais alto quer dizer usando mais ar na sua voz e por isso você acaba não usando as cordas vocais. Você tá perdendo o tom do música demais porque tem ar de mais que passa pelas suas cordas vocais. Claro que cantando em inglês também te afeta. Não é uma questão de fôlego, é uma questão não usar tanto ar nas cordas vocais. Você tem que aprender o básico de como esticar, conectar e usar as suas cordas vocais, bem do começo mesmo. Isso é uma coisa de que você realmente precisa da ajuda de alguém com você para poder te monitorar. O seu timbre, eu não sou a melhor pessoa para descrever isso. O seus hábitos vocais são bem semelhantes ao JYP, por exemplo. Eu gosto de você estar se soltando mais, mas também acho que você não faz muitas escolhas boas musicalmente. Para um menino, cantar uma música como a primeira que você mandou ou uma música da Britney Spears não é exatamente uma boa idéia. Ambos vocês parecem tar cantando uma música grave demais para vocês, ambos tem problema com tom e com ar, isso são só por maus hábitos vocais. Nada que sem ajuda não de para arrumar. Ele parece ser barítono, mas você eu fico na dúvida. E eu faço o que eu posso, eu queria poder ajudar mais na verdade.</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-39011\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=39011&amp;_wpnonce=3b68a62727\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-39011\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"reply\"><a rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"comment-reply-link\" href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?replytocom=39011#respond\" onclick=\"return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-39011&quot;, &quot;39011&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;130&quot; Starting from the fourth note you weren’t matching the pitch anymore and you only got exactly back on pitch around 0:18, so try to be more careful and aware. Slide more. </p>\n<p>As for the two note exercise, try to drop the jaw more and make the sound a bit more like Ah, a little less like Oh/Uh. It needs to be more opened, more forward. You did fine until the end, try to do it even slower to really work on the stretch and placement of the sound. And the last one shouldn’t have been a semitone, so be careful with that, okay? ^ ^ Thank you for posting the exercises, it helps me help you.</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-39072\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=39072&amp;_wpnonce=b0645202c0\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-39072\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"reply\"><a rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"comment-reply-link\" href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?replytocom=39072#respond\" onclick=\"return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-39072&quot;, &quot;39072&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;130&quot; )\" aria-label=\"Reply to ahmin3\">Reply</a></div>\t\t\t</article><!-- .comment-body -->\n</li><!-- #comment-## -->\n</ol><!-- .children -->\n</li><!-- #comment-## -->\n\t\t<li id=\"comment-39061\" class=\"comment even thread-even depth-1 parent highlander-comment\">\n\t\t\t<article id=\"div-comment-39061\" class=\"comment-body\">\n\t\t\t\t<footer class=\"comment-meta\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-author vcard\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt=\"\" src=\"https://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e99fb7c2b025258dbc7631aa47494d7b?s=74&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=G\" class=\"avatar avatar-74 grav-hashed grav-hijack\" height=\"74\" width=\"74\" id=\"grav-e99fb7c2b025258dbc7631aa47494d7b-0\">\t\t\t\t\t\t<b class=\"fn\">JohnnyL</b> <span class=\"says\">says:</span>\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-author -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-metadata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-39061\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-19T02:38:31+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 19, 2017 at 2:38 am\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>hello ahmin,<br>\ncould you talk about placement and projection?<br>\nthis is your explanation:<br>\nProjection : To project means to have your voice be heard. For the voice to travel, echo through a room and for it to have enough sound that people can hear it.</p>\n<p>Placement : To place your sound means to use the air and sound that comes from your vocal cords and focus it on certain areas of your body like your chest, head or mask so that they can amplify the sound. A chest placement will create a thicker, lower, bassier sound, a headier placement has more treble and a mask placement is the closest to the mouth. </p>\n<p>1)Can we say projection is focusing the voice? and how can we focus our voice? what are the muscle working(related to CT/TA)?<br>\n2) When we place our sound in chest/head/mask, what are the muscle doing? what are the different?<br>\n3) when we are throaty, what are the muscle doing? (using the other wrong muscle?)<br>\n4) nasal is soft palate lifting no enough and nasal placement? any other reason? nasal will cause unsupported? and what are the different between nasal/mask placement(someone say it is same)?<br>\n5) throat placement is placed too low without support. compare with chest placement, which one is lower? can we say a chest placement without support as throat placement?</p>\n<p>I’m sorry that i have so many questions since i’m interested in these knowledge.<br>\nI hope i have not make trouble for you.<br>\nthank you very much^^</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-39061\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=39061&amp;_wpnonce=4ab19ead5e\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-39061\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"reply\"><a rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"comment-reply-link\" href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?replytocom=39061#respond\" onclick=\"return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-39061&quot;, &quot;39061&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;130&quot; )\" aria-label=\"Reply to JohnnyL\">Reply</a></div>\t\t\t</article><!-- .comment-body -->\n<ol class=\"children\">\n\t\t<li id=\"comment-39062\" class=\"comment byuser comment-author-ahmin3 odd alt depth-2 parent highlander-comment\">\n\t\t\t<article id=\"div-comment-39062\" class=\"comment-body\">\n\t\t\t\t<footer class=\"comment-meta\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-author vcard\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt=\"\" src=\"https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/02dcf75f6bd3999e2cb9fe85ab48cf6e?s=74&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=G\" class=\"avatar avatar-74 grav-hashed grav-hijack\" height=\"74\" width=\"74\" id=\"grav-02dcf75f6bd3999e2cb9fe85ab48cf6e-22\">\t\t\t\t\t\t<b class=\"fn\">ahmin3</b> <span class=\"says\">says:</span>\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-author -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-metadata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-39062\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-19T02:53:34+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 19, 2017 at 2:53 am\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>1. Projection is irrelevant to the muscles because it will happen with every muscle working. It happens in the chest voice, the mixed voice, the head voice, the falsetto register, the whistle register. It’s to do with volume, not with muscle coordination.<br>\n2. I think you misunderstand what muscles mean. The muscles are the muscles IN the vocal cords. The muscles are ALWAYS working in the vocal cords as long as you’re singing, but of course it depends on what register you’re singing. So CT or TA, it depends on what register you’re in. So the muscles in your throat should be doing nothing, ideally.<br>\n3. When you’re throaty, the muscles in the vocal cords (TA/CT) aren’t the ones that cause the problems, but the swallowing muscles in your throat around your larynx.<br>\n4. No, nasality does not mean someone’s singing is unsupported. If that were the case, half of the average vocalists and even average to above average vocalists would have no supported ranges. Nasality takes away from projection, resonance and openness, not support. Nasal resonance is what some people call mask resonance, I don’t like the term because then it confuses people when trying to differentiate nasality from mask resonance.<br>\n5. Throat placement usually means the sound is also not fully placed in the mask nor lips at all, meaning the sound is pulled back and isn’t projecting well. Chest placement mixes with mask placement to an extent to mix, so it’s not about the placement that’s lower or higher than the other when it comes to chest vs throat, but where the sound is in relation to the mouth/lips.</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-39062\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=39062&amp;_wpnonce=6da5685ebd\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-39062\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"reply\"><a rel=\"nofollow\" Her throat isn’t very opened throughout, so she lacks roundness. She sounds really edgy throughout. She does have a very nice tone. 3:19 just strained high larynx quality, her throat closed more on the E5.”</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-39083\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=39083&amp;_wpnonce=c31bb49d51\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-39083\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"reply\"><a rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"comment-reply-link\" href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?replytocom=39083#respond\" onclick=\"return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-39083&quot;, &quot;39083&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;130&quot; -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>As a baritone, I don’t think you should be singing a girl group somewhat uptempo or even mid tempo song, the song is not built for your voice. You have quite a bit of tongue and jaw tension, you have pretty nice pitch but this song is not written for your voice so the range is too narrow and you are singing like a soprano down the octave, C4 is not that high for us. You lack support and you push from your throat, because it’s as if you’re trying to make C4 as high for you as C5 is for a soprano. Careful with the nasality as well.</p>\n<p id=\"comment-like-39156\" data-liked=\"comment-not-liked\" class=\"comment-likes comment-not-liked\"><a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?like_comment=39156&amp;_wpnonce=f7b31cebd6\" class=\"comment-like-link needs-login\" rel=\"nofollow\" data-blog=\"115589781\"><span>Like</span></a><span id=\"comment-like-count-39156\" class=\"comment-like-feedback\">Like</span></p>\n\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-content -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"reply\"><a rel=\"nofollow\" class=\"comment-reply-link\" href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/?replytocom=39156#respond\" onclick=\"return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-39156&quot;, &quot;39156&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;130&quot; )\" aria-label=\"Reply to ahmin3\">Reply</a></div>\t\t\t</article><!-- .comment-body -->\n<ol class=\"children\">\n\t\t<li id=\"comment-39171\" class=\"comment even depth-3 parent highlander-comment\">\n\t\t\t<article id=\"div-comment-39171\" class=\"comment-body\">\n\t\t\t\t<footer class=\"comment-meta\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-author vcard\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt=\"\" src=\"https://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c39fc45770d79459b3d592b4d2498b52?s=74&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=G\" class=\"avatar avatar-74 grav-hashed grav-hijack\" height=\"74\" width=\"74\" id=\"grav-c39fc45770d79459b3d592b4d2498b52-1\">\t\t\t\t\t\t<b class=\"fn\">Elias</b> <span class=\"says\">says:</span>\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-author -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-metadata\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"https://kpopvocalanalysis.net/comment-page-43/#comment-39171\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<time datetime=\"2017-04-21T08:44:45+00:00\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tApril 21, 2017 at 8:44 am\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</time>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div><!-- .comment-metadata -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</footer><!-- .comment-meta -->\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"comment-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<p>Thanks for your input!
